2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Incident Root-Cause: Grafana Dashboard Migration Field Config Loss

## Your Task

A Grafana dashboard migration (v38) silently drops table panel field override configuration during import. Dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` lose column widths and text alignment. Trace this bug to its root cause in the Grafana codebase. Find: 1. The Go source files under `pkg/services/dashboardimport/` or `pkg/services/dashboards/` that implement the v38 schema migration. 2. The specific function that handles `fieldConfig` merging and the conditional logic that fails for missing `defaults.custom`. 3. The schema version constant file that registers v38. Report the repo, file path, function name, and the flawed conditional expression for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
```

40-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed my analysis of the Grafana dashboard migration v38 bug. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause:** The v38 dashboard migration silently drops table panel field override configuration when panels lack explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` objects.

**Primary Bug Location:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`, line 116
- The conditional `if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok` checks if defaults exists and is a map
- When defaults is missing or malformed, this check fails, and while `migrateOverrides()` is still called, the fieldConfig structure is left in an invalid state

**Secondary Bug Location:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`, line 611  
- Uses the same flawed conditional pattern
- When a panel originally had `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`, the cleanup code tries to preserve it via `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag
- If the conditional fails (defaults missing), the code falls through to `delete(panel, prop)`, **permanently removing the entire fieldConfig**
- This causes loss of column widths, text alignment, and other field override configurations

**The Flawed Conditional Expression:**
```go
if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
```

This fails silently when `fieldConfig["defaults"]` is absent or not a map, causing preservation logic to be skipped and the entire fieldConfig to be deleted.

I've created the detailed findings in `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant file paths, function names, and the specific conditional expressions involved in the bug.

The problem arises because the migration doesn't guarantee that fieldConfig.defaults exists after processing, leaving it in a potentially invalid state.\\n\\n**Secondary Issue (frontend_defaults.go, line 611):** During dashboard cleanup in the filterDefaultValues function, the same flawed conditional appears: `if defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\\\"defaults\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok`. However, if defaults is missing or not a map, the condition fails and the code falls through to `delete(panel, prop)`, permanently removing the entire fieldConfig structure. This is the direct cause of the lost column widths and text alignment settings stored in field overrides.\\n\\n**The flawed conditional expression:** Both instances use `fieldConfig[\\\"defaults\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok` to check if defaults exists and is a map. This fails silently when defaults is absent, causing the subsequent preservation logic to be skipped. The correct approach would require either: (1) inverting the condition to `!ok` to handle missing defaults, or (2) explicitly checking for and initializing missing defaults before attempting to access its properties.\\n\\n**Impact:** Dashboards without explicit fieldConfig.defaults.custom lose all field override configurations (including custom.displayMode, columnWidth, textAlignment) during v38 migration because the cleanup phase discards the fieldConfig when it fails to validate the defaults structure.\\n\\n**Files and Functions Involved:**\\n- apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go: V38() function and processPanelsV38() (line 116 conditional)\\n- apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go: GetMigrations() registers V38 at line 74\\n- apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go: filterDefaultValues() function (line 611 conditional) and trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom() which tracks the _originallyHadFieldConfigCustom flag used in the problematic conditional check\"\n}\n",
